scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sanjuan.pr">sanjuan<wbr />.pr</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>San Juan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/hw/: &#39;wh&#39; in &#39;why&#39;">hw</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;sa\xc5\x8b<span class="wrap"> </span>\xcb\x88xwan&#93;</a></span>; Spanish for "Saint <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John</a>") is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> and most populous <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._insular_area)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. insular area)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Unincorporated territory">unincorporated territory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. As of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">2020 census</a>, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">57th-largest</a> city under the jurisdiction of the United States, with a population of 342,259. San Juan was founded by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> colonists in 1521, who called it <i><b>Ciudad de Puerto Rico</b> ("City of Puerto Rico"</i>, Spanish for <i>rich port city</i>).\n</p><p>Puerto Rico\'s capital is the second oldest European-established capital city in the Americas, after <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, founded in 1496,<sup id="cite_ref-SJCOPRI_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SJCOPRI-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_settlements_by_year_of_foundation" title="List of North American settlements by year of foundation">oldest</a> European-established city under <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="United States of America">United States sovereignty</a>. Several historical buildings are located in the historic district of <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>; among the most notable are the city\'s former <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="City Wall of San Juan">defensive walls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">Fort San Felipe del Morro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(San_Juan)" title="Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (San Juan)">Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, the oldest <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">executive mansion</a> in continuous use in the Americas. <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza_and_San_Juan_National_Historic_Site_in_Puerto_Rico" title="La Fortaleza and San Juan National Historic Site in Puerto Rico">These historic sites</a> were declared a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, San Juan is <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Port">Puerto Rico\'s most important seaport</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is the island\'s financial, cultural, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Tourism in Puerto Rico">tourism center</a>. The population of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo metropolitan area">metropolitan statistical area</a>, including San Juan and the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Can%C3%B3vanas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Can\xc3\xb3vanas, Puerto Rico">Can\xc3\xb3vanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Alta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Alta, Puerto Rico">Toa Alta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>, is about 2.443&#160;million inhabitants; thus, about 76% of the population of Puerto Rico now lives and works in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> San Juan is also a principal city of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_metropolitan_area#Combined_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan-Caguas-Fajardo Combined Statistical Area</a>. The city has been the host of events within the sports community, including the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>; 1966 <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>; events of the 2006, 2009 and 2013 <a href="/wiki/World_Baseball_Classic" title="World Baseball Classic">World Baseball Classics</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/MLB" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB">MLB</a> San Juan Series in 2010.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Timeline of San Juan, Puerto Rico">Timeline of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>.</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian era"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> people were the original inhabitants of the area before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">Europeans</a> to the island of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> in 1493. Remains of a small indigenous fishing village have been found in <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_San_Juan" title="Puerta de Tierra, San Juan">Puerta de Tierra</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard_Museum" title="Puerto Rico National Guard Museum">Puerto Rico National Guard Museum</a> stands today, however most archaeological sites in the region have been destroyed and lost throughout the colonial history.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The area of San Juan used to be the boundary between the tribal regions (yucayeques) of <i>Guaynabo</i> and <i>Haimanio</i>, led by the chiefs (<a href="/wiki/Caciques_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Caciques in Puerto Rico">caciques</a>) <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mabo_(cacique)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mabo (cacique) (page does not exist)">Mabo</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yuisa_(cacique)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yuisa (cacique) (page does not exist)">Yuisa</a> (also known as Loa\xc3\xadza), respectively, at the time of the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">Spanish conquistadors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Founding">Founding</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Founding"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/220px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/330px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG/440px-Ponce_de_Leon_house.JPG 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="576" /></a><figcaption>The ruins of <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>\'s residence at <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site">Caparra</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 1508, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a> founded the original settlement which he called <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site"><b>Caparra</b></a>. It was named after a <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1parra" title="C\xc3\xa1parra">former Roman city</a> in the province of <a href="/wiki/Caceres_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caceres (province)">C\xc3\xa1ceres</a> in Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_de_Ovando" title="Nicol\xc3\xa1s de Ovando">Nicol\xc3\xa1s de Ovando</a>, then the Governor of Spain\'s Caribbean territories.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Viejo,_Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pueblo Viejo, Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Pueblo Viejo</a> district of <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaynabo">Guaynabo</a>, directly to the west of the modern municipality of San Juan. A year later, the settlement was moved to a site then called <b>Puerto Rico</b>, Spanish for "rich port" or "good port", after its similar geographical features to the town of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Puerto Rico de Gran Canaria">Puerto Rico de Gran Canaria</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Caparra_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caparra-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_San_Juan_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of San Juan de Puerto Rico">local Catholic diocese</a>, the second oldest in the Americas and the oldest in the United States, was founded in the newly built settlement on August 8 of 1511.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1521, the newer settlement was given its formal name: <i><b>Ciudad de Puerto Rico de San Juan Bautista</b></i>. Many of the oldest European-founded institutions in the Western Hemisphere, such as the <a href="/wiki/Galer%C3%ADa_Nacional" title="Galer\xc3\xada Nacional">Santo Tom\xc3\xa1s de Aquino Convent</a> and the Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n Hospital, were established during this time in San Juan.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The ambiguous use of <i>San Juan Bautista</i> and <i>Puerto Rico</i> for both the city and the island in time led to a reversal in practical use by most inhabitants: by 1746 the name for the city (Puerto Rico) had become that of the entire island, leading to the city being identified as <i>Puerto Rico de Puerto Rico</i> on maps of the era.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HistoryS.J._18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoryS.J.-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spanish_Colonial_era">Spanish Colonial era</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish Colonial era"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Captaincy General of Puerto Rico">Captaincy General of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>San Juan, as a settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, was used by merchant and military ships traveling from Spain as the first stopover in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. Because of its prominence in the Caribbean, a network of fortifications was built to protect the transports of gold and silver from the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> to Europe. Because of the rich cargoes, San Juan became a target of the foreign powers of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Staat_van_Amerika,_map_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico,_1766.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/220px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/330px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg/440px-Staat_van_Amerika%2C_map_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_1766.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6476" data-file-height="4378" /></a><figcaption>San Juan and bay, Puerto Rico, 1766</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan underwent attacks from the English led by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Francis_Drake" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Francis Drake">Sir Francis Drake</a> in 1595 (in what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Puerto Rico">Battle of Puerto Rico</a>) and by <a href="/wiki/George_Clifford,_3rd_Earl_of_Cumberland" title="George Clifford, 3rd Earl of Cumberland">George Clifford, Earl of Cumberland</a>, in 1598. Artillery from San Juan\'s fort, <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Felipe_del_Morro" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a>, repelled Drake; however, Clifford managed to land troops and lay siege to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-history_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After a few months of English occupation, Clifford was forced to abandon the siege when his troops began to suffer from exhaustion and sickness. In 1625 the city was sacked by Dutch forces led by Captain <a href="/wiki/Boudewijn_Hendricksz" title="Boudewijn Hendricksz">Balduino Enrico</a> (also known as Boudewijn Hendricksz/Bowdoin Henrick), but El Morro withstood the assault and was not taken. The Dutch were counterattacked by Captain <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Am%C3%A9zqueta" title="Juan de Am\xc3\xa9zqueta">Juan de Am\xc3\xa9zqueta</a> and 50 members of the civilian militia on land and by the cannons of the Spanish troops in El Morro castle. The land battle left 60 Dutch soldiers dead and Enrico with a sword wound to his neck which he received from the hands of Am\xc3\xa9zqueta.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (January 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Dutch ships at sea were boarded by Puerto Ricans who defeated those aboard. After a long battle, the Spanish soldiers and volunteers of the city\'s militia were able to defend the city from the attack and save the island from an invasion. On October 21, Enrico set <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a> and the city ablaze. Captains Am\xc3\xa9zqueta and Andr\xc3\xa9s Botello decided to put a stop to the destruction and led 200 men in an attack against the enemy\'s front and rear guard. They drove Enrico and his men from their trenches and into the ocean in their haste to reach their ships.<sup id="cite_ref-PRH_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRH-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Juan_(1797)" title="Battle of San Juan (1797)">attack</a> in 1797, during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">Sir Ralph Abercromby</a> (who had just conquered <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a>). His army laid siege to the city but was forced to withdraw in defeat as the Puerto Rican defenses proved more resilient than those of Trinidad. Various events and circumstances, including liberalized commerce with Spain, the opening of the island to immigrants as a direct result of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Decree_of_Graces_of_1815" title="Royal Decree of Graces of 1815">Royal Decree of Graces of 1815</a>, and the colonial revolutions, led to an expansion of San Juan and other Puerto Rican settlements in the late 18th and early 19th century.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Spanish-American_War">Spanish-American War</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spanish-American War"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_campaign" title="Puerto Rico campaign">Puerto Rico campaign</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg/220px-Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg/330px-Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg/440px-Bombardment_of_El_Morro_in_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="580" data-file-height="363" /></a><figcaption>Bombardment of <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a> in 1898</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On May 8, 1898, United States Navy ships, among them <a href="/wiki/USS_Detroit_(C-10)" title="USS Detroit (C-10)">USS&#160;<i>Detroit</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Indiana_(BB-1)" title="USS Indiana (BB-1)">USS&#160;<i>Indiana</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_New_York_(ACR-2)" title="USS New York (ACR-2)">USS&#160;<i>New York</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Amphitrite_(BM-2)" title="USS Amphitrite (BM-2)">USS&#160;<i>Amphitrite</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Terror_(BM-4)" title="USS Terror (BM-4)">USS&#160;<i>Terror</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Montgomery_(C-9)" title="USS Montgomery (C-9)">USS&#160;<i>Montgomery</i></a>, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Rear_Admiral_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rear Admiral (United States)">Rear Admiral</a> <a href="/wiki/William_T._Sampson" title="William T. Sampson">William T. Sampson</a> arrived at San Juan Bay.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SS_City_of_Paris_(1888)" title="SS City of Paris (1888)">USS&#160;<i>Yale</i></a> captured the Spanish freighter <i>Rita</i> in San Juan Bay, thus being the first hostile encounter between the warring sides in Puerto Rico. On May 9, <i>Yale</i> fought a brief battle with an <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_cruiser" class="mw-redirect" title="Auxiliary cruiser">auxiliary cruiser</a> of Spain, name unknown, resulting in a Spanish victory. Around this time, Captain <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Rivero_M%C3%A9ndez" title="\xc3\x81ngel Rivero M\xc3\xa9ndez">\xc3\x81ngel Rivero M\xc3\xa9ndez</a> was assigned the command of the Spanish forces in the fortress of <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(San_Juan)" title="Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (San Juan)">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a> in San Juan. On May 10, <i>Yale</i> returned to San Juan Bay, Rivero-M\xc3\xa9ndez ordered his men to open fire upon <i>Yale</i> using an Ordo\xc3\xb1ez 15-centimeter cannon, thus becoming the first attack against the Americans in Puerto Rico during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GHA_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>For his actions, Captain Rivero-M\xc3\xa9ndez was awarded the "Cruz de la Orden de M\xc3\xa9rito Militar" (The Cross of the Order of the Military Merit) first class.<sup id="cite_ref-GHA_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The residents of San Juan were furious with Rivero and blamed him for the destruction caused to their city by the American bombardments. Nothing came of those accusations and Capt. Rivero-M\xc3\xa9ndez was ordered to turn over the keys of all the military installations in San Juan to Captain Henry A. Reed of the U.S. Army after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> was signed.<sup id="cite_ref-GHA_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHA-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 25, General <a href="/wiki/Nelson_A._Miles" title="Nelson A. Miles">Nelson A. Miles</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica" class="mw-redirect" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a> (in southwestern Puerto Rico) with 3,300&#160;soldiers in what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Campaign">Puerto Rican Campaign</a>. The American troops found some resistance and engaged the Spanish and Puerto Rican troops in battle, the most notable of these the battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yauco" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Yauco">Yauco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Asomante" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Asomante">Asomante</a>. All military actions in Puerto Rico were suspended August 13, 1898, after President <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a> and French Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Jules_Cambon" title="Jules Cambon">Jules Cambon</a>, acting on behalf of the Spanish government, signed an <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">armistice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-COPRSAW_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COPRSAW-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Spain ceded the island to the United States later the same year by signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1898)" title="Treaty of Paris (1898)">Treaty of Paris</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="20th-century">20th-century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th-century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_Photographic_Company_(0766).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/220px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/330px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg/440px-Detroit_Photographic_Company_%280766%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1204" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Armas,_San_Juan" title="Plaza de Armas, San Juan">Plaza de Armas</a>, San Juan, ca. 1900</figcaption></figure><p><a href="/wiki/Camp_Las_Casas" title="Camp Las Casas">Camp Las Casas</a>, located in the district of <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>, served as the main training camp for the Puerto Rican soldiers prior to World War I and World War II; the majority of the men trained in this facility were assigned to the "Porto Rico Regiment of Infantry" which was renamed the <a href="/wiki/65th_Infantry_Regiment_(United_States)" title="65th Infantry Regiment (United States)">65th Infantry Regiment</a> of the United States Army by the Reorganization Act of June 4, 1920. The 65th Infantry was deactivated in 1956 and became the only unit ever to be transferred from an active Army component to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_National_Guard" title="Puerto Rico National Guard">Puerto Rico National Guard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PRR_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRR-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Marxuach" title="Te\xc3\xb3filo Marxuach">Te\xc3\xb3filo Marxuach</a> (retired as a Lieutenant Colonel), a native of <a href="/wiki/Arroyo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arroyo, Puerto Rico">Arroyo, Puerto Rico</a>, fired what is considered to be the first shot of World War I fired by the regular armed forces of the United States against any ship flying the colors of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USNI_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNI-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Marxuach, who was a member of the "Porto Rico Regiment of Infantry" and Officer of the Day, on March 25, 1915, opened fire on the <i>Odenwald</i>, an armed German supply vessel, when it was trying to force its way out of San Juan\'s bay.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The shots ordered by Lt. Marxuach were the first fired by the United States in World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1919, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Rigau_Carrera" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Rigau Carrera">F\xc3\xa9lix Rigau Carrera</a>, "El Aguila de Sabana Grande" (The Eagle from <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Grande, Puerto Rico">Sabana Grande</a>), the first Puerto Rican pilot, became the first native Puerto Rican to fly an aircraft in the island when he flew his <a href="/wiki/Curtiss_JN-4" class="mw-redirect" title="Curtiss JN-4">Curtiss JN-4</a> from Las Casas. At the time, the area was used by the military as an air base and it was also Puerto Rico\'s first commercial airport, and Rigau Carrera was allowed to perform his historic flight from the airfield.<sup id="cite_ref-EM_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EM-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Camp Las Casas was eventually closed down, and in 1950 a public housing project by the name of <a href="/wiki/Residencial_Las_Casas" title="Residencial Las Casas">Residencial Fray Bartolome de Las Casas</a> was constructed on its former location.\n</p><p>On January 2, 1947, the people of San Juan elected <a href="/wiki/Felisa_Rinc%C3%B3n_de_Gautier" title="Felisa Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier">Felisa Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier</a> (also known as Do\xc3\xb1a Fela) (1897\xe2\x80\x931994) as their mayor. Thus, she became the first woman to be elected as the mayor of a capital city in any of the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> era, she ordered the establishment of the island\'s first Civil Defense system under the directorship of Colonel <a href="/wiki/Gilberto_Jos%C3%A9_Marxuach" title="Gilberto Jos\xc3\xa9 Marxuach">Gilberto Jos\xc3\xa9 Marxuach</a> (Te\xc3\xb3filo\'s son).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Rinc\xc3\xb3n de Gautier served as mayor until January 2, 1969.\nOn October 30, 1950, San Juan was the scene of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Uprising">San Juan Uprising</a>, one of many uprisings which occurred in various towns and cities in Puerto Rico, by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party">Puerto Rican Nationalist Party</a> against the governments of Puerto Rico and the United States. Among the uprising\'s main objective was to attack La Fortaleza and the <a href="/wiki/Jose_V._Toledo_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Jose V. Toledo Federal Building and United States Courthouse">United States Federal Court House Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. The "La Fortaleza battle", which ensued between the nationalists and the police lasted 15 minutes and ended when four of the five attackers were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Page_2_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Page_2-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="21st-century">21st-century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st-century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Juan has experienced periods of both stagnation and development in the recent years. <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">Gentrification</a> has been noticeable in areas of the city such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lo%C3%ADza_Street&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lo\xc3\xadza Street (page does not exist)">Lo\xc3\xadza Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rita_(Hato_Rey)" title="Santa Rita (Hato Rey)">Santa Rita</a> in R\xc3\xado Piedras.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In recent years the city has been the location of multiple strikes and protests, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_in_Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="United States Navy in Vieques, Puerto Rico">2001 protests</a> against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> in the island municipality of <a href="/wiki/Vieques,_Puerto_Rico" title="Vieques, Puerto Rico">Vieques</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_University_of_Puerto_Rico_strikes" title="2010\xe2\x80\x932011 University of Puerto Rico strikes">2010 and 2011 University of Puerto Rico strikes</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Telegramgate" title="Telegramgate">2019 protests</a> against Governor <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rossell\xc3\xb3">Ricardo Rossell\xc3\xb3</a> which resulted in his resignation.\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> made a direct impact in Puerto Rico, causing widespread damage and a collapse of the infrastructure in San Juan and the rest of Puerto Rico. The damage caused in 2017 was extensive, affecting the electricity, potable water supplies, transportation, and communication, but significant progress had been made in the capital by April 2019, and particularly by October 2019. This was significant for tourism, which had rebounded by October of that year and was close to the pre-Maria era.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>San Juan today remains an important cultural, financial and industrial center not only of Puerto Rico but of the Caribbean region. As the biggest industrial center of Puerto Rico, it is the home of industries such as tobacco processors, breweries, refining facilities for petroleum and sugar, and distillers of rum as well as manufacturers of metal products, cement, pharmaceuticals, and clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Convention_Center" title="Puerto Rico Convention Center">Puerto Rico Convention Center</a>, opened in 2005, is the largest of its kind in the Caribbean and one of the most advanced in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_juan_pr.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/220px-San_juan_pr.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/330px-San_juan_pr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/San_juan_pr.jpg/440px-San_juan_pr.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="4096" /></a><figcaption>San Juan and its <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> from space</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan is located along the north-eastern coast of Puerto Rico in the Northern Plains region. It lies south of the Atlantic Ocean; north of <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. The city occupies an area of 76.93 square miles (199.2&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of which, 29.11 square miles (75.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (37.83%) is water. San Juan\'s main water bodies are <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Bay" title="San Juan Bay">San Juan Bay</a> and two natural lagoons, the <a href="/wiki/Condado_Lagoon" title="Condado Lagoon">Condado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laguna_San_Jos%C3%A9_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Laguna San Jos\xc3\xa9 (Puerto Rico)">San Jos\xc3\xa9</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At almost 1,030 feet (314 m) above sea level, the highest point in the municipality of San Juan is located on an unnamed hill on the <i>Morcelo</i> sector of <a href="/wiki/Caimito,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caimito, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Caimito</a>, close to the municipal border with <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The municipality of San Juan is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan metropolitan area</a>, particularly the highly urbanized municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Trujillo Alto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. These municipalities, together with <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, form what is locally referred to as the <i>\xc3\x81rea Metro</i>, the core of the wider San Juan metropolitan area. In total 41 municipalities are included in the entire metropolitan area extends throughout the island\'s northern coast and central eastern regions.<sup id="cite_ref-www.whitehouse.gov_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.whitehouse.gov-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Monthly_Climate_Normals_(1991-2020)_-_San_Juan_Area,_PR(ThreadEx).svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg/220px-Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="203" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg/330px-Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg/440px-Monthly_Climate_Normals_%281991-2020%29_-_San_Juan_Area%2C_PR%28ThreadEx%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="516" /></a><figcaption>Climate chart for San Juan</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">Am</a>) with year-round <a href="/wiki/Growing_season" title="Growing season">growing season</a>. It has an average temperature of 81.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F (27.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C). Temperatures of 90&#160;\xc2\xb0F (32&#160;\xc2\xb0C) or higher are seen on an average 79 days annually, more commonly occurring during the wetter months of the northern summer, especially if the winds come from the south.<sup id="cite_ref-NOWData_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the winter, temperatures can drop to around 60&#160;\xc2\xb0F (16&#160;\xc2\xb0C). The average winter low is 71&#160;\xc2\xb0F (22&#160;\xc2\xb0C). The coolest temperature officially recorded was 60&#160;\xc2\xb0F (16&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on March 3, 1957, and the hottest was 98&#160;\xc2\xb0F (37&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on October 9, 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-TWC_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TWC-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The record cold daily maximum is 71&#160;\xc2\xb0F (22&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on February 4, 1935. The record warm daily minimum is 83&#160;\xc2\xb0F (28&#160;\xc2\xb0C) on August 11, 1995, the most recent of four occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-NOWData_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>With a mean minimum of 67&#160;\xc2\xb0F (19 C), San Juan is in USDA plant <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zone</a> 13B, which is the highest category. Rainfall is well-distributed throughout the year. The months of January, February, and March are the driest. As March averages just 1.95 inches (49.5&#160;mm) of rain, the city falls under the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon</a> category.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Rainfall averages 56.35 inches (1,431.3&#160;mm), falling on an average 198.5 days per year.<sup id="cite_ref-NOWData_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite this dampness, the city averages 2,970 hours of sunshine per year, or just over <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1154941027">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac"><span class="num">2</span>&#8260;<span class="den">3</span></span> of the possible total.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAAsun_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAAsun-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Annual rainfall has historically ranged from 35.53&#160;in (902&#160;mm) in 1991 to 89.50&#160;in (2,273&#160;mm) in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-NOWData_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOWData-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Sahara_Dust_over_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="720" /></a><figcaption>June 2022 haze event caused by <a href="/wiki/Saharan_dust" title="Saharan dust">Saharan dust</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As with other parts of Puerto Rico and the Caribbean, San Juan is often blanketed by waves of <a href="/wiki/Saharan_dust" title="Saharan dust">Saharan dust</a> coming from the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> across the Atlantic Ocean in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">Northern Africa</a>. Although beneficial to the tropical environment,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> these dust storms have recently become hazardous to human health causing haze and overheating in urban areas of the island. Due to San Juan\'s relatively flat geography, the dust often settles in these flat coastal regions of Puerto Rico as its flow is blocked by the higher altitude <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a> to the south, causing intense episodes of haze to settle for long periods of time, especially during periods of more scarce rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Recent advancements include early warning systems to prepare the population for these intense episodes by both local authorities and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Maria_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Effects of Hurricane Maria in Puerto Rico">Effects of Hurricane Maria in Puerto Rico</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:170922-Z-BG835-909_(37348163586).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg/220px-170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg/330px-170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg/440px-170922-Z-BG835-909_%2837348163586%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136" /></a><figcaption>Department of Defense vehicles traveling through a major highway in San Juan flooded with the Hurricane Maria rainfall</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> made landfall in southeastern Puerto Rico on September 20, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Gusts of up to 113&#160;mph (182&#160;km/h) were reported in the capital city shortly before landfall in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa,_Puerto_Rico" title="Yabucoa, Puerto Rico">Yabucoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The municipality of San Juan experienced widespread flooding in most coastal areas, and roofs were blown off from numerous structures.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla</a> was largely destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the wider metropolitan area, flooding from <a href="/wiki/La_Plata_Lake" title="La Plata Lake">Lake La Plata</a> produced flash floods that trapped residents of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> the Juana Matos neighborhood was estimated to be 80% destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Sep21_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Sep21-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At least eight people died from the flooding, while many were unaccounted for.<sup id="cite_ref-ToaBaja_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToaBaja-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14"><style
