href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/data:Ncei.noaa.gov/weather/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.tab" class="extiw" title="commons:data:Ncei.noaa.gov/weather/San Juan, Puerto Rico.tab">raw graph data</a>.</small>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Beaches">Beaches</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Beaches"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Condado_Beach,_San_Juan,_PR,_USA.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg/220px-Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg/330px-Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg/440px-Condado_Beach%2C_San_Juan%2C_PR%2C_USA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Condado_Beach" title="Condado Beach">Condado Beach</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan is home to numerous <a href="/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_Puerto_Rico" title="List of beaches in Puerto Rico">beaches</a>, all of which are open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All beaches of San Juan face the Atlantic Ocean. The <a href="/wiki/Isleta_de_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="Isleta de San Juan">Islet of San Juan</a> hosts Los Cables Beach and La Perla Beach next to the <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> district of <a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla</a>, the Capitolio Beach located immediately north of the Puerto Rico Capitol, Puerta de Tierra Beach along the <i>Paseo de Puerta de Tierra</i>, and <a href="/wiki/El_Escambr%C3%B3n_Beach" title="El Escambr\xc3\xb3n Beach">El Escambr\xc3\xb3n Beach</a> at the northeastern edge of the islet. The latter is the most popular beach in the islet due to its shore being protected from the strong Atlantic Ocean waves by reefs that serve as natural <a href="/wiki/Breakwater_(structure)" title="Breakwater (structure)">breakwaters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From east to west, the beaches in Santurce include <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park_Beach" title="Ocean Park Beach">Ocean Park Beach</a> (also known as \xc3\x9altimo Trolley Beach), <a href="/wiki/Condado_Beach" title="Condado Beach">Condado Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Playita_del_Condado" title="Playita del Condado">Playita del Condado</a>. Ocean Park Beach and El Condado Beach are the largest in the city and they host a large number of hotels and businesses that cater to tourists and beachgoers.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Beach_erosion">Beach erosion</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Beach erosion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>As with other beaches across Puerto Rico and the Caribbean,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the beaches of San Juan are currently under the threat of <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">coastal erosion</a>, particularly that of Ocean Park.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The threat has become more evident recently and there are currently no state reports dedicated to the documentation or mitigation planning, according to oceanographer and geologist Maritza Barreto.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Parks">Parks</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Parks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The municipality of San Juan contains numerous parks, including public parks, historic and heritage parks, nature reserves, protected natural areas, and recreational parks. These parks are managed by a number of entities such as the Municipality, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Natural_and_Environmental_Resources" title="Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources">Puerto Rico Department of Natural and Environmental Resources</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservation_easement" title="Conservation easement">conservation easements</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="San_Juan_Ecological_Corridor">San Juan Ecological Corridor</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: San Juan Ecological Corridor"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Ecological_Corridor" title="San Juan Ecological Corridor">San Juan Ecological Corridor</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg/220px-University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg/330px-University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg/440px-University_of_Puerto_Rico_Botanical_Gardens_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1809" data-file-height="1206" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Botanical_Garden" title="San Juan Botanical Garden">University of Puerto Rico Botanical Garden</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <b>San Juan Ecological Corridor</b> is a conservation project by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">Government of Puerto Rico</a> consisting in 6 different units found within the municipality of San Juan: the Cupey Arboretum, which protects the <a href="/wiki/Riparian_zone" title="Riparian zone">riparian</a> ecosystems along the <a href="/wiki/Piedras_River_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Piedras River (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>; the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Do%C3%B1a_In%C3%A9s_Mendoza_Urban_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Do\xc3\xb1a In\xc3\xa9s Mendoza Urban Forest (page does not exist)">Do\xc3\xb1a In\xc3\xa9s Mendoza Urban Forest</a>, a small urban forest located next to the Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Foundation in <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Llana_Sur,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Llana Sur, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Sabana Llana Sur</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Capuchinos_Forest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Los Capuchinos Forest (page does not exist)">Los Capuchinos Forest</a>, a forest which covers a small <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> area also in Sabana Llana Sur; the <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Milenio_State_Forest" title="Nuevo Milenio State Forest">New Millennium State Forest</a>, one of the 20 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rico_state_forests" title="List of Puerto Rico state forests">state forests of Puerto Rico</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Old_Piedras_River_Aqueduct" title="Old Piedras River Aqueduct">San Juan Waterworks</a>, consisting of the Old Piedras River Aqueduct and adjacent <a href="/wiki/Historic_districts_in_the_United_States" title="Historic districts in the United States">historic district</a>; and the University of Puerto Rico Botanical Garden, also known as the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Botanical_Garden" title="San Juan Botanical Garden">San Juan Botanical Garden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Historical_parks">Historical parks</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Historical parks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_National_Historic_Site" title="San Juan National Historic Site">San Juan National Historic Site</a> is home to <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Morro_Esplanade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="El Morro Esplanade (page does not exist)">El Morro Esplanade</a>, a large open area located between <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ballaj%C3%A1,_Old_San_Juan" title="Ballaj\xc3\xa1, Old San Juan">Ballaj\xc3\xa1</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. The esplanade is located in the <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontory</a> which gives <i>El Morro</i> its name and it offers views of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Bay" title="San Juan Bay">San Juan Bay</a> and the rest of San Juan. It is very popular for activities such as picnics, <a href="/wiki/Amateur_astronomy" title="Amateur astronomy">stargazing</a><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kite" title="Kite">kite flying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The district of the <a href="/wiki/Capitol_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Capitol of Puerto Rico">Capitol of Puerto Rico</a> is home to the Iglesias Pant\xc3\xadn and Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Mar\xc3\xadn parks, and a line of monuments located along Constituci\xc3\xb3n Avenue which includes the <i>Walkway of the Presidents</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police" title="Puerto Rico Police">Puerto Rico Police</a> Memorial Monument and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a> Memorial Monument. The <i>Loma de los Vientos</i>, or <i>Loma del Viento</i> (Spanish for "hill of winds"), is a small open green area located northwest of the Capitol, next to <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(San_Juan)" title="Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (San Juan)">Castle San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>, and it often hosts events such as the <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany</a> celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Rivera_Park" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Park">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Park</a> is a 27.2 acre recreational and historic park located in <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_San_Juan" title="Puerta de Tierra, San Juan">Puerta de Tierra</a>, between Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera, <a href="/wiki/Avenida_Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Avenida Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a> and Constituci\xc3\xb3n avenues. It is the largest public square in Puerto Rico, and it is home to several historic sites such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Ger%C3%B3nimo_Powderhouse&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo Powderhouse (page does not exist)">Polvor\xc3\xadn San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo de Boquer\xc3\xb3n</a>, which used to supply gunpowder to the nearby <a href="/wiki/Fort%C3%ADn_de_San_Ger%C3%B3nimo" title="Fort\xc3\xadn de San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo">Fort\xc3\xadn de San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo</a>. The park used to host a small zoo, and currently hosts gazebos, gardens, restaurants and access to the beach. The park has been listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> since November 14, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Polvor%C3%ADn_de_Miraflores" title="Polvor\xc3\xadn de Miraflores">Polvorin de Miraflores</a> is a historic district and park located next to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Convention_Center" title="Puerto Rico Convention Center">Puerto Rico Convention Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Isla_Grande_(Santurce)" title="Isla Grande (Santurce)">Isla Grande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>. The ammunition storage house dates to the mid-18th century and it is also listed on the National Register of Historic Places.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Another historic district currently under revitalization is the <a href="/wiki/Old_Piedras_River_Aqueduct" title="Old Piedras River Aqueduct">San Juan Waterworks</a> historic district which contains the Old Piedras River Aqueduct. There are plans to revitalize the old aqueduct structures and its surroundings to create a historic park open to visitors and researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg/660px-El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="660" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg/990px-El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg/1320px-El_Morro_Old_San_Juan_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11547" data-file-height="2523" /></a><figcaption>El Morro Esplanade as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">castle</a> walls.</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Municipal_parks">Municipal parks</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Municipal parks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg/220px-La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg/330px-La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg/440px-La_Ventana_al_Mar_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="901" data-file-height="900" /></a><figcaption>Aerial view of <a href="/wiki/La_Ventana_al_Mar" title="La Ventana al Mar">Ventana al Mar</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Some of the recreational parks of the municipality include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bah%C3%ADa_Urbana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bah\xc3\xada Urbana (page does not exist)">Bah\xc3\xada Urbana</a>, a waterfront park located in Old San Juan and Puerta de Tierra by the San Juan Bay; the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paseo_de_Puerta_de_Tierra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paseo de Puerta de Tierra (page does not exist)">Paseo de Puerta de Tierra</a>, a recreational walkway along the Atlantic Ocean cliffs of Puerta de Tierra that connects the Puerto Rico Capitol with <a href="/wiki/El_Escambr%C3%B3n_Beach" title="El Escambr\xc3\xb3n Beach">El Escambr\xc3\xb3n Beach</a> and Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Park.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/La_Ventana_al_Mar" title="La Ventana al Mar">Ventana al Mar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Condado_Lagoon" title="Condado Lagoon">Laguna del Condado</a> Jaime Ben\xc3\xadtez Park, Parque del Indio are some of the parks located in <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">El Condado</a> district of Santurce. Dr. Jos\xc3\xa9 Celso Barbosa Park is located in <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park_(Santurce)" title="Ocean Park (Santurce)">Ocean Park</a>, also in Santurce. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Park_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Central Park (San Juan, Puerto Rico) (page does not exist)">Parque Central</a>, also known as the San Juan Municipal Central Park, is a large park and recreational complex located in southern Santurce near the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Nuevo_River" title="Puerto Nuevo River">Puerto Nuevo River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Pe%C3%B1a_Channel" title="Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Channel">Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Channel</a>. The Enrique Mart\xc3\xad Coll Linear Park connects the Central Park to <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1o_Mart%C3%ADn_Pe%C3%B1a_Nature_Reserve" title="Ca\xc3\xb1o Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Nature Reserve">Ca\xc3\xb1o Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Nature Reserve</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_Park" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Park">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Park</a>, La Merced Park, Dr. Jos\xc3\xa9 N. G\xc3\xa1ndara Park, Santiago Iglesias Pant\xc3\xadn Park are some of the parks located in Hato Rey.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Park is one of the largest in the municipality. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Gobernador_Pi%C3%B1ero,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero</a> district between Hato Rey and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Nuevo_(Hato_Rey)" title="Puerto Nuevo (Hato Rey)">Puerto Nuevo</a>. The park has gazebos that can be rented for events, green areas for strolls, biking and picnics, an artificial lake with paddleboats for rent ($6), and a number of playgrounds for children. Its main attraction is the <a href="/wiki/Cable_transport" title="Cable transport">cableway</a> that crosses the park and offers scenic views of the <a href="/wiki/Piedras_River_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Piedras River (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">Piedras River</a> and the city while providing transportation to the <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente_Coliseum" title="Roberto Clemente Coliseum">Roberto Clemente Coliseum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Nature_reserves">Nature reserves</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Nature reserves"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected areas of Puerto Rico">Protected areas of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>The municipality of San Juan is home to various important ecosystems and preserved natural areas. Some of the ecosystems of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan_Bay_National_Estuary&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Juan Bay National Estuary (page does not exist)">San Juan Bay National Estuary</a>, which is the only tropical estuary in the <a href="/wiki/National_Estuary_Program" title="National Estuary Program">National Estuary Program</a> network, are protected by numerous nature reserves and protected areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1o_Mart%C3%ADn_Pe%C3%B1a_Nature_Reserve" title="Ca\xc3\xb1o Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Nature Reserve">Ca\xc3\xb1o Mart\xc3\xadn Pe\xc3\xb1a Nature Reserve</a>. Other areas protected under the San Juan Bay National Estuary include <a href="/wiki/Condado_Lagoon" title="Condado Lagoon">El Condado Lagoon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Laguna_San_Jos%C3%A9_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Laguna San Jos\xc3\xa9 (Puerto Rico)">San Jos\xc3\xa9 Lagoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Boquer%C3%B3n_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" title="El Boquer\xc3\xb3n (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">El Boquer\xc3\xb3n</a> where the San Antonio Creek and the Condado Lagoon connect with the Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Two of the 20 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rico_state_forests" title="List of Puerto Rico state forests">state forests</a> of Puerto Rico are located in the municipality of San Juan: the <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Milenio_State_Forest" title="Nuevo Milenio State Forest">New Millennium Urban Forest</a>, which is also part of the San Juan Ecological Corridor, and the <a href="/wiki/San_Patricio_State_Forest" title="San Patricio State Forest">San Patricio Urban Forest</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_forest" title="Secondary forest">secondary forest</a> located next to a <a href="/wiki/Mogote" title="Mogote">mogote</a>. The Hermanas Sendra and San Juan Park Protected Natural Areas are located inland within the municipality of San Juan in the barrios of <a href="/wiki/Caimito,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caimito, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Caimito</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cupey,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cupey, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Cupey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Cityscape">Cityscape</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cityscape"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:719px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan,_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="General view of harbor at San Juan, Puerto Rico looking South to San Juan Bay, 1927. The clock tower building at center was the San Juan Rail Terminal."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/711px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg" decoding="async" width="711" height="250" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/1067px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg/1422px-General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan%2C_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7927" data-file-height="2787" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_view_of_harbor_at_San_Juan,_Porto_Rico_looking_South.jpg" title="File:General view of harbor at San Juan, Porto Rico looking South.jpg"> </a></div><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">General view of harbor at San Juan, Puerto Rico looking South to San Juan Bay, 1927. The clock tower building at center was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan_Railway_Station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Juan Railway Station (page does not exist)">San Juan Rail Terminal</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Architecture">Architecture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Architecture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in San Juan, Puerto Rico">National Register of Historic Places listings in San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerto_Rico_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/220px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/330px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Puerto_Rico_01.jpg/440px-Puerto_Rico_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1932" data-file-height="1235" /></a><figcaption>Old San Juan</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Miami_Building_Facade.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Miami_Building_Facade.JPG/220px-Miami_Building_Facade.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Miami_Building_Facade.JPG/330px-Miami_Building_Facade.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Miami_Building_Facade.JPG/440px-Miami_Building_Facade.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4752" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> <a href="/wiki/Miami_Building" title="Miami Building">Miami Building</a> on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ashford_Avenue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ashford Avenue (page does not exist)">Ashford Ave</a> in <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">Condado</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The architecture of San Juan is very diverse, due to its size and all the cultural influences received during its existence. The oldest part of the city, known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>, mostly features the influence of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_architecture" title="Spanish architecture">Spanish architecture</a>. This part of the city is comprised by a network of <a href="/wiki/Sett_(paving)" title="Sett (paving)">"setted" roads</a> usually surrounded by colonial, two-storied houses built on <a href="/wiki/Masonry" title="Masonry">masonry</a>. Some colonial structures have been restored and serve either as government offices or museums.<sup id="cite_ref-Grupo_Editorial_EPRL_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grupo_Editorial_EPRL-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some examples are the <a href="/wiki/Ballaj%C3%A1_Barracks" title="Ballaj\xc3\xa1 Barracks">Ballaj\xc3\xa1 Barracks</a>, which now serve as museum and headquarters of several cultural organizations; <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, which has served as the residence of the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">Governor of Puerto Rico</a> since the 16th Century; and the Ancient Welfare Asylum, which now houses the Institute of Puerto Rican Culture, among others. Old San Juan also features several public squares, like the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Armas,_San_Juan" title="Plaza de Armas, San Juan">Plaza de Armas</a>, located in front of San Juan City Hall; and cathedrals, like the <a href="/wiki/Catedral_Metropolitana_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_San_Juan_Bautista_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catedral Metropolitana Bas\xc3\xadlica de San Juan Bautista (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">Cathedral of San Juan Bautista</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Grupo_Editorial_EPRL_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grupo_Editorial_EPRL-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Old San Juan is also notable for being partly enclosed by <a href="/wiki/City_Wall_of_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="City Wall of San Juan">massive walls</a> and fortifications built by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish government">Spanish government</a>. The colonial Walls of the city of San Juan had five gates. The main was the Puerta de San Juan, today preserved, built in 1635. It also had the Puerta de San Jos\xc3\xa9, the Puerta de Santa Rosa, the Puerta de San Justo and the Puerta de Santiago, the latter built between 1635 and 1641 by Spanish Captain General \xc3\x8d\xc3\xb1igo de la Mota Sarmiento.\n</p><p>The architecture is more varied in other districts of the city, and the different <a href="/wiki/Spanish_architecture" title="Spanish architecture">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecture of the United States">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rican_architects" title="List of Puerto Rican architects">Puerto Rican</a> construction styles that reflect the historic architecture trends are most evident in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_San_Juan" title="Puerta de Tierra, San Juan">Puerta de Tierra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pueblo, San Juan, Puerto Rico">downtown R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mid-century_modern" title="Mid-century modern">Mid-Century Modern</a> being the most popular styles.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many of the buildings that best exemplify these architectural trends in San Juan are also inscribed in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings" title="United States National Register of Historic Places listings">United States National Register of Historic Places</a> (NRHP), such as the <a href="/wiki/Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Lourdes_Chapel" title="Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Lourdes Chapel">Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Lourdes Chapel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a>, 1907),<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Antiguo_Casino_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Antiguo Casino de Puerto Rico">Antiguo Casino de Puerto Rico</a> (<a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux-Arts</a>, 1917),<sup id="cite_ref-nrhpdoc_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrhpdoc-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Normandie_Hotel" title="Normandie Hotel">Normandie Hotel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>, 1942),<sup id="cite_ref-NRIS_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRIS-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_Building_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Supreme Court Building (Puerto Rico)">Puerto Rico Supreme Court Building</a> (<a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">Modern</a>, 1955).<sup id="cite_ref-nrhpinv3_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrhpinv3-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The University of Puerto Rico, R\xc3\xado Piedras Campus is also home to a rich variety of buildings that showcase the history of Puerto Rican architecture throughout the past 120 years, with buildings designed by notable architects such as <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a>\'s student <a href="/wiki/Henry_Klumb" title="Henry Klumb">Henry Klumb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_H._Bennett" title="Edward H. Bennett">Edward H. Bennett</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_E._Parsons" title="William E. Parsons">William E. Parsons</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Carmoega" title="Rafael Carmoega">Rafael Carmoega</a> who designed the distinctive <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Tower" title="Roosevelt Tower">clock tower</a> and the <a href="/wiki/The_Quadrangle_(University_of_Puerto_Rico,_R%C3%ADo_Piedras)" title="The Quadrangle (University of Puerto Rico, R\xc3\xado Piedras)">university quadrangle</a>, both of which were inscribed in the NRHP in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-:03_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:03-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of San Juan, Puerto Rico">Subdivisions of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg/220px-Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="mw-file-element" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg/440px-Map_of_San_Juan_Districts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1628" data-file-height="1632" /></a><figcaption>The subdivisions of San Juan</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_and_Rio_Piedras_municipalities_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/San_Juan_and_Rio_Piedras_municipalities_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-San_Juan_and_Rio_Piedras_municipalities_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4e/San_Juan_and_Rio_Piedras_municipalities_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="673" /></a><figcaption>San Juan and Rio Piedras as separate municipalities on a 1915 map</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As with the other Puerto Rican municipalities, San Juan is administratively divided into <i><a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>.</i> What is now known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> occupied the western end of a rocky islet, the <a href="/wiki/Isleta_de_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="Isleta de San Juan">Isleta de San Juan</a>, at the mouth of San Juan Bay. During the 20th century, the main population centers surged well beyond the walls of the old city and onto Puerto Rico\'s main island and merged with the existing settlements east and south of Old San Juan. Together with <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_San_Juan" title="Puerta de Tierra, San Juan">Puerta de Tierra</a>, Old San Juan comprises the barrio of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Antiguo" title="San Juan Antiguo">San Juan Antiguo</a>.\n</p><p>With the annexation of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a> in 1951, the municipality of San Juan grew to four times its previous size. As a result, the municipality also went from 2 to 18 barrios (barrios),<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 16 of which fall within the former municipality of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>. Eight of the 18 barrios are further subdivided into subbarrios, including the two barrios (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Antiguo" title="San Juan Antiguo">San Juan Antiguo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>) that belonged to the original municipality of San Juan.\n</p><p>The 18 barrios are:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Caimito,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caimito, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Caimito</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cupey,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cupey, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Cupey</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Cinco,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="El Cinco, San Juan, Puerto Rico">El Cinco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gobernador_Pi%C3%B1ero,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey_Central,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Hato Rey Central, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Hato Rey Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey_Norte,_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="Hato Rey Norte, San Juan">Hato Rey Norte</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey_Sur,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Hato Rey Sur, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Hato Rey Sur</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Monacillo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Monacillo, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Monacillo</a></li>\n<li><a Juan, Puerto Rico">Oriente</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pueblo, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Pueblo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Arenas,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" Norte</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabana_Llana_Sur,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Llana Sur, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Sabana Llana Sur</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Antiguo" title="San Juan Antiguo">San Juan Antiguo</a> (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Old San Juan, Puerto Rico">Old San Juan</a>, a historic district within the barrio)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tortugo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Tortugo, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Tortugo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Universidad,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Universidad, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Universidad</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="San_Juan_Antiguo">San Juan Antiguo</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: San Juan Antiguo"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_San_Juan" title="Puerta de Tierra, San Juan">Puerta de Tierra, San Juan</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Juan_3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/220px-San_Juan_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/330px-San_Juan_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Juan_3.jpg/440px-San_Juan_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="773" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>Some streets in Old San Juan are still paved with blue <a href="/wiki/Cobblestones" class="mw-redirect" title="Cobblestones">cobblestones</a> from the Spanish colonial era</figcaption></figure>\n<p>During the Spanish colonial times most of the urban population resided in what is today known as <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>. This sector is located on the western half of a small island called the <a href="/wiki/Isleta_de_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="Isleta de San Juan">Isleta de San Juan</a>, which is connected to the mainland by two bridges and a <a href="/wiki/Causeway" title="Causeway">causeway</a>. The small island, which comprises an area of 47 square miles (120&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), also hosts the working-class neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerta de Tierra">Puerta de Tierra</a> and most of Puerto Rico\'s <a href="/wiki/Executive_Departments_of_the_Government_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive Departments of the Government of Puerto Rico">central government</a> buildings, including the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Capitol" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Capitol">Commonwealth\'s Capitol</a>. This is also the largest and most populated <i>subbarrio</i> of San Juan Antiguo.<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The main central part of the old city is characterized by narrow streets made of blue <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobblestone</a> and picturesque colonial buildings, some of which date back to the 16th and 17th century. Sections of the old city are surrounded by massive walls and several defensive structures and notable forts. These include the 16th-century <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Felipe_del_Morro" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort San Felipe del Morro">Fort San Felipe del Morro</a> and the 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(San_Juan)" title="Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (San Juan)">Fort San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>, both part of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_National_Historic_Site" title="San Juan National Historic Site">San Juan National Historic Site</a>, and the 16th-century <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">El Palacio de Santa Catalina</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a>, which serves as the governor\'s mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other buildings of interest predating the 18th century are the <i>Ayuntamiento or Alcald\xc3\xada</i> (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan_City_Hall" title="San Juan City Hall">San Juan City Hall</a>), the <i>Diputaci\xc3\xb3n Provincial</i> and the <i>Real Intendencia</i> buildings, which house the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_State" title="Puerto Rico Department of State">Puerto Rico Department of State</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rosa" title="Casa Rosa">Casa Rosa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Church" title="San Jos\xc3\xa9 Church">San Jos\xc3\xa9 Church</a> (1523) and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Hotel_El_Convento" title="Hotel El Convento">Hotel El Convento</a>, the former house of the Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n family known as <a href="/wiki/Casa_Blanca_(San_Juan)" title="Casa Blanca (San Juan)">Casa Blanca</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Tapia" title="Teatro Tapia">Teatro Tapia</a>, the former Spanish barracks (now <a href="/wiki/Ballaj%C3%A1_Barracks" title="Ballaj\xc3\xa1 Barracks">Museum of Ballaj\xc3\xa1</a>), <i>La Princesa</i> (former municipal jail, now headquartering the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_Magdalena_de_Pazzis_Cemetery" title="Santa Mar\xc3\xada Magdalena de Pazzis Cemetery">Santa Mar\xc3\xada Magdalena de Pazzis Cemetery</a>, located just outside the city walls.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Catedral_Metropolitana_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_San_Juan_Bautista_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catedral Metropolitana Bas\xc3\xadlica de San Juan Bautista (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">Cathedral of San Juan Bautista</a> (construction began in the 1520s) is also located in Old San Juan and contains the tomb of the Spanish explorer and settlement founder <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Old San Juan, also known as the "old city", is the main cultural tourist attraction in Puerto Rico; its bayside is lined by dock slips for large <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Santurce">Santurce</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Santurce"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-La_Placita_de_Santurce_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/La_Placita_de_Santurce" title="La Placita de Santurce"><i>La Placita</i></a> in Santurce (2020).</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue,_Condado,_Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Highrise_on_Ashford_Avenue%2C_Condado%2C_Santurce%2C_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1891" data-file-height="2847" /></a><figcaption>Highrises on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ashford_Avenue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ashford Avenue (page does not exist)">Ashford Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">El Condado</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Santurce is the largest and most populated barrio in the municipality of San Juan, and one of the most densely populated areas of the island (13,257.4 persons per square mile).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Santurce, originally named <i>San Mateo de Cangrejos</i> (Saint Matthew of the Crabs), was a settlement for <a href="/wiki/Freedman" title="Freedman">freed African slaves</a> during the early days of the city. After Pablo Ubarri Capetillo, a Spanish railroad developer and <i>Count of San Jos\xc3\xa9 de Santurce</i> under the Spanish colonial period, sought permission to link San Juan with R\xc3\xado Piedras proper via steam tramway in 1878, the time it took to travel between both points were shortened and thereby stimulated the colonization and growth of the district. At the beginning of the twentieth century an electric trolley was installed, the township was split into three parts, and its main settlement, merged with the city, was renamed using the Spanish spelling of <a href="/wiki/Santurtzi" title="Santurtzi">Santurtzi</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a></i> in Basque), Ubarri\'s birthplace in <a href="/wiki/Biscay" title="Biscay">Vizcaya</a>, Spain. The "Museo de Arte de Puerto Rico" (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Museum_of_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Museum of Art">Puerto Rico Museum of Art</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and other important cultural venues are located in Santurce.\n</p><p>This barrio is further divided into subbarrios such as the tourist-oriented neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">Condado</a>, which occupies land that used to be owned by Ubarri Capetillo. Beaches such as nearby <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park_(Santurce)" title="Ocean Park (Santurce)">Ocean Park</a>, popular with swimmers, <a href="/wiki/Surfers" class="mw-redirect" title="Surfers">surfers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kitesurfers" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitesurfers">kitesurfers</a>, are found all along the district\'s Atlantic coastline which is also the locus of numerous hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miramar_(Santurce)" title="Miramar (Santurce)">Miramar</a> is mainly a residential area rising south of the Condado Lagoon. It comprises the former <i><a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrio</a></i> of Miraflores, as well as drained marshland and landfill over which was built San Juan\'s first airport, the Isla Grande airport, which was renamed <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport">Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport</a> in honor of Major <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas-Dominicci" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernando Luis Ribas-Dominicci">Fernando Luis Ribas-Dominicci</a> (USAF). Miramar now hosts the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Convention_Center" title="Puerto Rico Convention Center">Puerto Rico Convention Center</a> as well as some of San Juan Harbor\'s cruise ship piers. In 2005 Miramar was designated an historical district of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="R\xc3\xado_Piedras"><span id="R.C3.ADo_Piedras"></span>R\xc3\xado Piedras</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: R\xc3\xado Piedras"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia,_R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_San_Juan.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg/220px-Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg/330px-Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg/440px-Plaza_de_la_Convalecencia%2C_R%C3%ADo_Piedras%2C_San_Juan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5275" data-file-height="2967" /></a><figcaption>Plaza de la Convalecencia in <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pueblo, San Juan, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras Pueblo</a> (the historic downtown of Rio Piedras).</figcaption></figure>\n<p>South of Santurce is <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>, part of the former municipality of R\xc3\xado Piedras. Hato Rey was grazing ground for cattle owned by the royal government (hence its name, the <i>King\'s Herd</i> in Spanish) as early as the 16th century,<sup id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is now considered the financial center of the island. A section of this district is often referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Milla_de_Oro" title="Milla de Oro">Milla de Oro</a></i> (actually 0.47 miles or 0.76 kilometers long) due in part to the many banks and businesses located there.<sup id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the southern part of the city is the socially diversified community of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>. Founded in the mid-1850s, R\xc3\xado Piedras was a separate town which hosted sugar cane plantations and the estates of some of San Juan\'s wealthiest inhabitants (as well as their working-class staff). The Spanish colonial governors also had their summer home there on land which eventually gave way to the main campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a>. In 1951 the municipalities of San Juan and R\xc3\xado Piedras were merged to redefine San Juan\'s current city limits. Today R\xc3\xado Piedras comprises the largest area of the municipality of San Juan.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is home to the "Plaza del Mercado" (R\xc3\xado Piedras <a href="/wiki/Marketplace" title="Marketplace">Marketplace</a>), the main campus and the Medical Sciences campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Botanical_Garden" title="San Juan Botanical Garden">San Juan Botanical Garden</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<table class="wikitable floatright">\n<caption>Race \xe2\x80\x93 San Juan, Puerto Rico \xe2\x80\x93 2020 Census<sup id="cite_ref-109" Rican</b></td>\n<td>75,864</td>\n<td>22.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a>/<a R\xc3\xado Piedras</caption><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid var(--color-base, #000000);padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid style="text-align:right;padding:1px">18,880</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+37.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1920 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">24,745</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+31.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1930 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">40,853</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+65.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1940 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">68,290</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+67.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1950 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">134,989</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+97.7%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">332,344</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+146.2%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The municipality of San Juan has a population of 342,259 as of the 2020 US Census, making it the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">largest in Puerto Rico</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-poptotal_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poptotal-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">57th largest in the United States and its territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From 1899 to 1950 the municipality of San Juan excluded the township of R\xc3\xado Piedras. For this reason, population data and land area for the period make reference only to the Antiguo San Juan and Santurce <i>barrios</i>, or subdivisions, of San Juan. The old municipality of R\xc3\xado Piedras constituted the third most populated city of Puerto Rico at the time of its annexation in 1951. Its strategic location south of the capital served as a junction for all the principal ways of transportation of the island and as a geographical entry to San Juan, which are factors that prompted R\xc3\xado Piedras\'s dramatic urban development in the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>, the racial composition of San Juan was as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White</a>: 68.0% (<a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">Non-Hispanic Whites</a>: 1.2%)</li>\n<li>Black or African American: 18.3% (Non-Hispanic Blacks: 0.3%)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a>: 0.8%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian</a>: 0.4%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">Native Hawaiian</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a>: 0.0%</li>\n<li>Some other race: 8.2%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 4.0%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race): 98.2%</li></ul>\n<p>Among the Hispanic and Latino population, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Ricans</a> are the largest group; they make up 87.5% of San Juan\'s Hispanic population. People of <a href="/wiki/Dominican_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Dominican American">Dominican</a> descent make up 7.6% of the Hispanic population, while those of <a href="/wiki/Cuban_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuban American">Cuban</a> descent form 1.7% of the Hispanic populace. Other Hispanic and Latino groups collectively form 3.2% of San Juan\'s Hispanic population.\n</p><p>There are 4,822 whites and 1,187 blacks of non-Hispanic origin living in San Juan. Non-Hispanic whites and blacks form 1.2% and 0.3% of San Juan\'s population respectively. There are also approximately 673 Asians of non-Hispanic origin in San Juan; they make up less than 0.1% of the population. However, Asians of Hispanic and non-Hispanic origin together number at 6,342.<sup id="cite_ref-American_FactFinder_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_FactFinder-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The vast majority of Asians in San Juan are of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese American">Chinese</a> descent; of the 6,342 Asians, 4,928 are Chinese. Chinese comprise 1.4% of the population. The only other sizable Asian group in San Juan are <a href="/wiki/Indian_Americans" title="Indian Americans">Indian Americans</a>; there are 698 people of Indian descent in the city, forming 0.2% of the population. There are very small numbers of people of <a href="/wiki/Filipino_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino American">Filipino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese American">Japanese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Vietnamese American">Vietnamese</a> ancestry; none of these groups number more than 100 members.<sup id="cite_ref-American_FactFinder_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_FactFinder-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2006\xe2\x80\x932008 American Community Survey, 87.5% of San Juan\'s population was native and 12.5% were foreign-born. Of the native population, 86.9% were born in Puerto Rico or the U.S. proper, of which 75.6% were born in Puerto Rico and 8.9% were born in the U.S. The other 0.7% were born in a different U.S. territory or born abroad to American parents. The remaining 11.9% of the population were born outside the United States and U.S. territories.\n</p><p>In recent years, an increasing number of Americans not of Hispanic ancestry (both of <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> and of <a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White American</a> descent) have moved to San Juan. In addition, a large number of <a href="/wiki/Stateside_Puerto_Ricans" title="Stateside Puerto Ricans">Stateside Puerto Ricans</a> have settled in the city upon their return to Puerto Rico. There is also a growing <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> population, both of Hispanic and non-Hispanic origin.\n</p><p>San Juan today is home to the largest <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Puerto_Rico" title="History of the Jews in Puerto Rico">Jewish community in Puerto Rico</a>, and one of the largest Jewish communities in the Caribbean,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with more than 2,000 people attending two local synagogues in <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Judaism" title="Conservative Judaism">Conservative</a> Shaare Zedeck Synagogue and the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">Reform</a> Temple Beth Shalom)<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an additional synagogue (the <a href="/wiki/Chabad_affiliated_organizations" title="Chabad affiliated organizations">Chabad</a> Jewish Center of Puerto Rico) in <a href="/wiki/Isla_Verde,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isla Verde, Puerto Rico">Isla Verde</a> in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In terms of ancestry, 23,875 people claimed American ancestry, which is equivalent to 5.8% of San Juan\'s population. Other sizable ancestry groups included those of <a href="/wiki/Italian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian American">Italian</a> descent, <a href="/wiki/French_American" class="mw-redirect" title="French American">French</a> descent, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> descent. People of Italian descent numbered at 1,694, forming 0.4% of the population; people of French descent numbered at 1,064, forming 0.2% of the population. Finally, those of West Indian descent numbered at 1,393, forming 0.3% of San Juan\'s population. Approximately 1,026 people claimed <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> ancestry; 719 claimed <a href="/wiki/Irish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish American">Irish</a> ancestry; 646 claimed <a href="/wiki/German_American" class="mw-redirect" title="German American">German</a> ancestry; 431 claimed <a href="/wiki/Arab_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab American">Arab</a> ancestry, and 346 claimed <a href="/wiki/English_American" class="mw-redirect" title="English American">English</a> ancestry. There are many other ancestry groups in San Juan, but they are very scant.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2000, speakers of <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as a first language accounted for 12.93% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Popular_Center_(01).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg/220px-Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg/330px-Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg/440px-Popular_Center_%2801%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Popular,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Popular, Inc.">Popular, Inc.</a> headquarters at Popular Center in <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan experienced significant economic growth following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. During this period the city underwent an industrial revolution, although as of 1984 it had never generated its own economic region.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city\'s economy relies mostly on companies dedicated to the manufacture of several products, including: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemical substances</a> (bleach and house cleaning products); pharmaceuticals; rum and other beverages; <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a>; electric tools; <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronic devices</a>; plastics, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textiles</a>, and food-based products.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is also a key industry, based on San Juan\'s proximity to Puerto Rico\'s main airport, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nThe tourism focus of the city is located in the district of Condado Beach where there are luxurious hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Historical locations such as El Morro, Old San Juan and El Cuartel de Ballaja are promoted in tourism campaigns. The district of Hato Rey contains a corporate sector known as <a href="/wiki/Milla_de_Oro" title="Milla de Oro">Milla de Oro</a> (Golden Mile) which serves as the headquarters of local and international banks. San Juan\'s Hato Rey district is often referred to as the "Wall Street of the Caribbean", due to the influence of the area on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean\'s economy.<sup id="cite_ref-mini-wall-street_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-wall-street-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>San Juan is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Popular,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Popular, Inc.">Popular, Inc.</a>, parent company of <a href="/wiki/Banco_Popular_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Banco Popular de Puerto Rico">Banco Popular de Puerto Rico</a>, Popular Bank, <a href="/wiki/E-Loan" title="E-Loan">E-Loan</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_1000" title="Fortune 1000">Fortune 1000</a> company as of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other companies based in San Juan include <a href="/wiki/ATH_(interbank_network)" title="ATH (interbank network)">ATH Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_BanCorp" title="First BanCorp">First BanCorp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Puerto_Rico" title="Liberty Puerto Rico">Liberty Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Cervantes_Group" title="The Cervantes Group">The Cervantes Group</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Triple-S_Management_Corporation" title="Triple-S Management Corporation">Triple-S Management Corporation</a>. <a href="/wiki/Seaborne_Airlines" title="Seaborne Airlines">Seaborne Airlines</a> is headquartered on the ninth floor of the World Plaza Building in Hato Rey.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Tourism">Tourism</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Street_art,_statues_in_Old_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Street_art%2C_statues_in_Old_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3126" data-file-height="1770" /></a><figcaption><i>Fuente Ra\xc3\xadces</i>, <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_La_Princesa" class="mw-redirect" title="Paseo de La Princesa">Paseo de La Princesa</a></figcaption></figure><p>Technological advances after World War II in the development of the airliner, coupled with the island\'s climate and natural setting, have transformed San Juan into the springboard for tourism around the island, and has made the rest of the Caribbean known throughout the world during the last fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today the capital features hotels, museums, historical buildings, restaurants, parks, beaches and shopping centers.\n</p><p>Old San Juan is often emphasized in tourism campaigns, promoting the historic nature of its colonial buildings and narrow streets covered by cobblestones, a blue stone cast from furnace slag; they were brought over as ballast on Spanish ships.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This includes the city\'s ancient defensive wall and forts, most notably <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Felipe_del_Morro" title="Castillo San Felipe del Morro">El Morro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Castillo_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(San_Juan)" title="Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal (San Juan)">Castillo San Crist\xc3\xb3bal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On January 23, 1984, both of these edifices together with <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort%C3%ADn_San_Juan_de_la_Cruz" title="Fort\xc3\xadn San Juan de la Cruz">El Ca\xc3\xb1uelo</a> (in nearby <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>) were included as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> catalogued as being part of humanity\'s cultural patrimony as part
