of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a>-administered <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_National_Historic_Site" title="San Juan National Historic Site">San Juan National Historic Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The restaurants and art galleries in the zone are visited by tourists and locals alike.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_121-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="284" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Bacardi_building_in_Cata%C3%B1o%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3346" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Rum" title="Cathedral of Rum">Casa Bacardi</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> is a popular tourist attraction for those visiting San Juan.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Outside of Old San Juan, the Puerto Rico Convention Center District (PRCC) includes the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Convention_Center" title="Puerto Rico Convention Center">Puerto Rico Convention Center</a>, which hosts a number of local and international events throughout the year such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puerto_Rico_Comic_Con&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puerto Rico Comic Con (page does not exist)">Puerto Rico Comic Con</a>, the biggest of its kind in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Distrito_T-Mobile" title="Distrito T-Mobile">PRCC District</a> also hosts a number of hotels, nightclubs, shops, cinemas, bars and restaurants,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Music_Hall" title="Coca-Cola Music Hall">Coca-Cola Music Hall</a>, and the Toro Verde Eco Adventure Park.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other notable tourist attractions in San Juan include the <a href="/wiki/Condado_Beach" title="Condado Beach">Condado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Park_Beach" title="Ocean Park Beach">Ocean Park Beaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Escambr%C3%B3n_Beach" title="El Escambr\xc3\xb3n Beach">El Escambr\xc3\xb3n</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fort%C3%ADn_de_San_Ger%C3%B3nimo" title="Fort\xc3\xadn de San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo">Fort\xc3\xadn de San Ger\xc3\xb3nimo</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Placita_de_Santurce" title="La Placita de Santurce">La Placita de Santurce</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferr%C3%A9_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center">Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_Park" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Park">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Rivera_Park" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Park">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Am%C3%A9ricas_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas (Puerto Rico)">Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Outlets_at_Montehiedra" title="The Outlets at Montehiedra">The Outlets at Montehiedra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%B1orial_Plaza" title="Se\xc3\xb1orial Plaza">Se\xc3\xb1orial Plaza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Mall_of_San_Juan" title="The Mall of San Juan">The Mall of San Juan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Art_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Museum of Art of Puerto Rico">Museum of Art of Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Museum_of_Contemporary_Art" title="Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art">Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Vida_Silvestre" title="Museo de Vida Silvestre">San Juan Wildlife Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Botanical_Garden" title="San Juan Botanical Garden">University of Puerto Rico Botanical Garden</a>, among others. The University of Puerto Rico\'s main campus in R\xc3\xado Piedras is also of interest with its <a href="/wiki/The_Quadrangle_(University_of_Puerto_Rico,_R%C3%ADo_Piedras)" title="The Quadrangle (University of Puerto Rico, R\xc3\xado Piedras)">historic quadrangle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Tower" title="Roosevelt Tower">clock tower</a>, its number of theaters and venues which host events such as the <a href="/wiki/Casals_Festival" title="Casals Festival">Casals Festivals</a>, and a museum. San Juan is also used by tourists as a base to explore other attractions within and outside the San Juan metropolitan area, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bacardi" title="Bacardi">Bacardi</a> <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Rum" title="Cathedral of Rum">Cathedral of Rum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o_barrio-pueblo" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o barrio-pueblo">boardwalk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, the "Pork Highway" of <a href="/wiki/Guavate,_Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guavate, Cayey, Puerto Rico">Guavate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bioluminiscent_bay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bioluminiscent bay (page does not exist)">bioluminiscent bay</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fajardo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Fajardo, Puerto Rico">Fajardo</a>, the beaches and street food of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pi%C3%B1ones_(Lo%C3%ADza,_Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pi\xc3\xb1ones (Lo\xc3\xadza, Puerto Rico) (page does not exist)">Pi\xc3\xb1ones</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza,_Puerto_Rico" title="Lo\xc3\xadza, Puerto Rico">Lo\xc3\xadza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/El_Yunque_National_Forest" title="El Yunque National Forest">El Yunque National Forest</a> recreational areas in the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Luquillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Luquillo, Puerto Rico">Luquillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Grande, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Grande</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Post_Hurricane_Maria">Post Hurricane Maria</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Post Hurricane Maria"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>An April 2019 report indicated that, by that time, repairs after Hurricane Maria were moving rapidly. Only a few hotels were still closed in San Juan and that life for tourists in and around the capital had, for the most part, returned to normal.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By October 2019, nearly all of the popular amenities for tourists, in the major destinations such as San Juan, Ponce and Arecibo, were in operation on the island and tourism was rebounding. This was important for the economy, since tourism provides up 10% of Puerto Rico\'s GDP, according to Discover Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In late November 2019, reports indicated that 90 calls to San Juan by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_Cruises_Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Caribbean Cruises Ltd.">Royal Caribbean</a> ships would be cancelled during 2020 and 2021. This step would mean 360,000 fewer visitors, with a loss to the island\'s economy of $44&#160;million. As well, 30 ship departures from San Juan were being canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Arts and culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_notable_residents_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="List of notable residents of San Juan, Puerto Rico">List of notable residents of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg/220px-Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg/330px-Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg/440px-Centro_de_Bellas_Artes_Luis_Ferre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferr%C3%A9_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center">Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan is the birthplace of artists and musicians who have significantly influenced Puerto Rican culture. During the 20th century, the musical aspect of the city was influenced by performers including <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_Americans" title="West Indian Americans">Afro-Caribbean</a> dancer and choreographer <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_del_Villard" title="Sylvia del Villard">Sylvia del Villard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Pedreira" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Enrique Pedreira">Jos\xc3\xa9 Enrique Pedreira</a> who became a composer of Puerto Rican <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Puerto_Rico#Danza" title="Music of Puerto Rico"><i>Danzas</i></a>. International musicians such as opera singer <a href="/wiki/Justino_D%C3%ADaz" title="Justino D\xc3\xadaz">Justino D\xc3\xadaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Ram\xc3\xb3n Ayala</a> (Daddy Yankee) and <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Martin" title="Ricky Martin">Ricky Martin</a> were born in the city. Other notable residents include writers <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Braschi" title="Giannina Braschi">Giannina Braschi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Blanco_(writer)" title="Tom\xc3\xa1s Blanco (writer)">Tomas Blanco</a>, award-winning actors <a href="/wiki/Raul_Julia" title="Raul Julia">Raul Julia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benicio_del_Toro" title="Benicio del Toro">Benicio del Toro</a>, and comedian <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot</a>. Teacher <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Cordero_(educator)" title="Rafael Cordero (educator)">Rafael Cordero</a> (1790\xe2\x80\x931868), was influential in the development of Puerto Rican education and began the process of beatification in 2013, if accepted as a saint he will become only the second black saint from the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Performing arts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferr%C3%A9_Performing_Arts_Center" title="Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center">Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Performing Arts Center</a> (Spanish: <i>Centro de Bellas Artes Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9</i>) hosts some of the most important musical and artistic events in Puerto Rico. It is home to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Puerto Rico Symphony Orchestra">Puerto Rico Symphony Orchestra</a> (PRSO) and hosts the <a href="/wiki/Casals_Festival" title="Casals Festival">Casals Festival</a>, the most important classical music festival in the Caribbean. The venue also hosts theater and musical performances such as <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(musical)" title="Hamilton (musical)">Hamilton</a>, which it hosted in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The Conservatory of Music of Puerto Rico is a public music conservatory that hosts Puerto Rican and international students has a longstanding relationship with the classical music movement in the island. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><span lang="es" style="font-style: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Ateneo_Puertorrique%C3%B1o" title="Ateneo Puertorrique\xc3\xb1o">Ateneo Puertorrique\xc3\xb1o</a></span></span> and the theater of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico,_R%C3%ADo_Piedras_Campus" title="University of Puerto Rico, R\xc3\xado Piedras Campus">University of Puerto Rico, Rio Piedras</a> also host important music events.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Museums">Museums</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Museums"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce,_San_Juan.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg/220px-Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg/330px-Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg/440px-Museo_de_Arte_de_Puerto_Rico_en_Santurce%2C_San_Juan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5140" data-file-height="3859" /></a><figcaption>Puerto Rico Museum of Art</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city is also the home of contemporary and classic art museums. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Art_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Museum of Art of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico Museum of Art</a> hosts the largest collection of art in Puerto Rico, housing over 1,100 permanent art pieces and displaying temporary exhibitions containing artwork from various locations through Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Museum_of_Contemporary_Art" title="Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art">Puerto Rico Museum of Contemporary Art</a>, located in Santurce, specializes in contemporary artwork from Latin America and the Caribbean. The paintings displayed in the permanent exhibition are either acquired by the museum\'s administrative personnel or donated by artists and collectors. They are judged by a panel of painters, art critics, and scholars before being displayed.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Casals_Museum" title="Pablo Casals Museum">Pablo Casals Museum</a>, the San Juan Book Museum, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Museum_of_the_Americas_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Museum of the Americas (San Juan, Puerto Rico) (page does not exist)">Museum of the Americas</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Galer%C3%ADa_Nacional" title="Galer\xc3\xada Nacional">National Gallery</a> display historic items and artwork alongside contemporary art.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miscellaneous museums such as the Children\'s Museum, the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Vida_Silvestre" title="Museo de Vida Silvestre">San Juan Wildlife Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bacardi" title="Bacardi">Bacardi</a> Distillery (also known as the "Rum Cathedral") in nearby <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o" class="mw-redirect" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> appeal to different audiences through interactive exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Casa_Dra._Concha_Melendez_Ramirez" title="Casa Dra. Concha Melendez Ramirez">Casa Dra. Concha Melendez Ramirez</a> in Santurce is a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a> and museum and research center that showcases the life and work of <a href="/wiki/Concha_Mel%C3%A9ndez" title="Concha Mel\xc3\xa9ndez">one of the most important figures</a> in the literary culture of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-nhl_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nhl-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> is also home to important art museums, such as the <a href="/wiki/Galer%C3%ADa_Nacional" title="Galer\xc3\xada Nacional">Puerto Rico National Gallery</a>, and numerous private art galleries.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of San Juan, Puerto Rico">List of mayors of San Juan, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Structure">Structure</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Structure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="273" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_San_Juan%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="363" data-file-height="451" /></a><figcaption>Present coat of arms of San Juan</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As one of Puerto Rico\'s 78 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipalities</a>, San Juan\'s government consists of two branches, the executive and the legislative. Those citizens eligible to vote directly elect the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_San_Juan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of San Juan">Mayor of San Juan</a> and the municipal assembly for four-year terms. The municipal government is housed in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_City_Hall" title="San Juan City Hall">City Hall</a> or <i>Casa Alcaldia</i>, which is located at 153 San Francisco Street, facing the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Armas,_San_Juan" title="Plaza de Armas, San Juan">Plaza de Armas</a> at the center of <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcald\xc3\xada_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcald\xc3\xada-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> City Hall was constructed based on <a href="/wiki/Madrid,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid, Spain">Madrid</a>\'s City Hall starting in 1604 and finally completed in 1789.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcald\xc3\xada_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcald\xc3\xada-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The executive branch is headed by a popularly elected mayor. The office is held by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Romero" title="Miguel Romero">Miguel Romero Lugo</a> who won in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2020">2020 general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Romero" title="Miguel Romero">Miguel Romero Lugo</a> took over from <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Yul%C3%ADn_Cruz" title="Carmen Yul\xc3\xadn Cruz">Carmen Yul\xc3\xadn Cruz</a>, who was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2012">2012 general election</a>. Before her, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_A._Santini" class="mw-redirect" title="Jorge A. Santini">Jorge A. Santini</a> held the position for 12 years. In addition to running the city\'s day-to-day operations and supervising associated departments, the mayor is responsible for appointing a secretary-auditor and a treasurer. San Juan\'s Municipal Legislature is made up of 17 municipal legislators, elected at-large, which represent the city\'s population.<sup id="cite_ref-Asamblea_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asamblea-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Coat_of_arms_and_flag">Coat of arms and flag</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Coat of arms and flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Torres_Vargas" title="Diego de Torres Vargas">Diego de Torres Vargas</a></div><figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_(Puerto_Rico)-Spanish_Rule.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/160px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png" decoding="async" width="160" height="242" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/240px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg/320px-Historic_Coat_of_Arms_of_San_Juan_%28Puerto_Rico%29-Spanish_Rule.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="298" data-file-height="451" /></a><figcaption>Historic coat of arms of San Juan (Spanish rule).</figcaption></figure><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 8, 1948, the city government of San Juan officially adopted as the city\'s first flag an orange field, in the center of which is the coat of arms of the city. The orange color was based and taken from Father <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Torres_Vargas" title="Diego de Torres Vargas">Diego de Torres Vargas</a>\' text and it reads:\n</p><p>"<i>Escudo de armas dado a Puerto Rico por los Reyes Cat\xc3\xb3licos en el a\xc3\xb1o de 1511, siendo Procurador un vecino llamado Pedro Moreno. Son&#160;: un cordero blanco con su banderilla colorada, sobre un libro, y todo sobre una isla verde, que es la de Puerto Rico, y por los lados una F y una I, que quiere decir Fernando e Isabel, los Reyes Cat\xc3\xb3licos que se las dieron, y hoy se conservan en el estandarte real, que es de damasco anaranjado, con que se gan\xc3\xb3 la ciudad</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>("Coat of arms given to Puerto Rico by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a> in the year 1511 being Procurator a <i>vecino</i> (citizen) named Pedro Moreno. They are a white lamb with a red flag, on top of a book, and everything above a green island, which is Puerto Rico...which is of orange damask, with which the city was won"). It appears that the color was changed from orange to white at some point.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Territorial_and_federal_government">Territorial and federal government</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Territorial and federal government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_(28755163211).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg/220px-Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg/330px-Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg/440px-Capitolio_de_Puerto_Rico_%2828755163211%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Capitol_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Capitol of Puerto Rico">Capitol of Puerto Rico</a>, built between 1921 and 1929.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan is the territorial capital of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Commonwealth of Puerto Rico</a>, and it is home to the <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch_of_the_government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Executive branch of the government of Puerto Rico">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico">legislative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Judiciary of Puerto Rico">judicial</a> branches of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican government</a>. San Juan is also the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district I">Puerto Rico Senatorial district I</a>, which is represented by two Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Puerto_Rico" title="United States District Court for the District of Puerto Rico">United States District Court for the District of Puerto Rico</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>. There are two additional federal offices in the San Juan metropolitan area: the <a href="/wiki/Jose_V._Toledo_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Jose V. Toledo Federal Building and United States Courthouse">Jose V. Toledo U.S. Post Office and Courthouse</a> in Old San Juan and the GSA Federal Center in Guaynabo.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI), along with other federal organisms, has also had regional offices at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Federico_Degetau_Federal_Building&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Federico Degetau Federal Building (page does not exist)">Federico Degetau Federal Building</a> also in Hato Rey.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Safety">Safety</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Safety"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Law enforcement in San Juan is the joint responsibility of the Department of Police and Public Safety, also known as the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Police_Department" title="San Juan Police Department">San Juan Police Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Police Department">Puerto Rico Police Department</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Municipal Police, originally known as the "San Juan Municipal Guard", was created in 1521 and had active military and law enforcement functions until 1980, when Act #77 created municipal law enforcement agencies in Puerto Rico. It employs over 1,000 sworn officers plus civilian staff.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Crime">Crime</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Crime"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In 2010 there were 201 homicides in San Juan, a rate of around 50 per 100,000 residents. In 2019 they were 172 homicides a rate of 53 per 100,000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 2019 bulletin ranking of the 50 most violent cities in the world San Juan ranked as the 16th most violent in the world with a rate of 54.01 murders per 100,000 inhabitants,<sup id="cite_ref-seguridadjusticiaypaz_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seguridadjusticiaypaz-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the 3rd most violent in the United States and its territories after <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Media">Media</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Media of Puerto Rico">Media of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Newspapers">Newspapers</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Newspapers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Most of Puerto Rico\'s major newspapers are published in San Juan: <a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_D%C3%ADa" title="El Nuevo D\xc3\xada">El Nuevo D\xc3\xada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primera_Hora_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Primera Hora (Puerto Rico)">Primera Hora</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Vocero" title="El Vocero">El Vocero</a> and the English-language <a href="/wiki/The_San_Juan_Star" class="mw-redirect" title="The San Juan Star">San Juan Star</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other newspapers published in San Juan are <a href="/wiki/Metro_Newspapers" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro Newspapers">Metro Puerto Rico</a>, Indice and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Business">Caribbean Business News</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Radio">Radio</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Radio"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Juan is also home to several of Puerto Rico\'s major radio stations: <a href="/wiki/WKAQ_(AM)" title="WKAQ (AM)">WKAQ 580 AM</a> and <a href="/wiki/WKAQ-FM" title="WKAQ-FM">105 FM</a>, WPRM Salsoul 99.1 FM, WODA La Nueva 94 FM, Fidelity 95.7 FM, WSKN Radio Isla 1320 AM, WORO Radio Oro 92.5 FM, Salsa Hits Radio, WAPA Radio, WOYE Magic 97.3, WRTU Radio Universidad FM, WIPR 940 AM, Mix 107.7 FM, WTOK Hot 102, AZ Rock, Radio Antillas, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Television">Television</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Television"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Some of the television stations based in San Juan are <a href="/wiki/WKAQ-TV" title="WKAQ-TV">WKAQ-TV</a> <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">Telemundo</a>/<a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Univision_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Univision Puerto Rico">WORA Univision Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/WAPA-TV" title="WAPA-TV">WAPA-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/WIPR-TV" title="WIPR-TV">WIPR-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mega_TV_(American_TV_network)" title="Mega TV (American TV network)">WTCV Mega TV</a>, WJPX <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_TeV%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Am\xc3\xa9rica TeV\xc3\xa9">Am\xc3\xa9rica TeV\xc3\xa9</a>, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Movies_and_filming">Movies and filming</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Movies and filming"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>San Juan has been the setting of numerous movies and the city has also been used as a stand-in or substitute for other cities and countries where filming is more expensive, more dangerous or more restrictive. Some of the most popular movies filmed in San Juan are: <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Bananas_(film)" title="Bananas (film)">Bananas</a></i> (1971), <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Ron" title="Captain Ron">Captain Ron</a></i> (1992), <i><a href="/wiki/Assassins_(1995_film)" title="Assassins (1995 film)">Assassins</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/Amistad_(film)" title="Amistad (film)">Amistad</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Boys_II" title="Bad Boys II">Bad Boys II</a></i> (2003) standing-in as <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Dancing:_Havana_Nights" title="Dirty Dancing: Havana Nights">Dirty Dancing: Havana Nights</a></i> (2004) also as <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Men_Who_Stare_at_Goats_(film)" title="The Men Who Stare at Goats (film)">The Men Who Stare at Goats</a></i> (2009) standing-in as <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Losers_(2010_film)" title="The Losers (2010 film)">The Losers</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Five" title="Fast Five">Fast Five</a></i> (2011) standing-in as <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides</a></i> (2011) standing-in as <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="C\xc3\xa1diz">C\xc3\xa1diz, Spain</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rum_Diary_(film)" title="The Rum Diary (film)">The Rum Diary</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/22_Jump_Street" title="22 Jump Street">22 Jump Street</a></i> (2014) standing-in as a Mexican resort, <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America:_Civil_War" title="Captain America: Civil War">Captain America: Civil War</a></i> (2016) standing-in as <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">Lagos, Nigeria</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Force_of_Nature_(2020_film)" title="Force of Nature (2020 film)">Force of Nature</a></i> (2020), <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther:_Wakanda_Forever" title="Black Panther: Wakanda Forever">Black Panther: Wakanda Forever</a></i> (2022), and <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Beetle_(film)" title="Blue Beetle (film)">Blue Beetle</a></i> (2023).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/220px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/330px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg/440px-Torre_Universidad_de-Puerto_Rico_Rio_Piedras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Tower" title="Roosevelt Tower">main tower</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="University of Puerto Rico">University of Puerto Rico</a> campus in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan is home to many of Puerto Rico\'s institutions of higher learning. The <a href="/wiki/UPRRP" class="mw-redirect" title="UPRRP">University of Puerto Rico R\xc3\xado Piedras Campus</a> is located in San Juan, along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico,_Medical_Sciences_Campus" title="University of Puerto Rico, Medical Sciences Campus">University of Puerto Rico\'s Medical Sciences Campus</a>. Other colleges located in San Juan are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Sacred_Heart_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="University of the Sacred Heart (Puerto Rico)">University of the Sacred Heart</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Polytechnic University of Puerto Rico">Polytechnic University of Puerto Rico</a>, the Ana G. M\xc3\xa9ndez University System\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_University_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan University (Puerto Rico)">Metropolitan University</a>, the Metropolitan Campus of the <a href="/wiki/Inter_American_University_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter American University of Puerto Rico">Inter American University of Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Albizu_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Albizu University">Carlos Albizu University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Evangelic_Seminary_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelic Seminary of Puerto Rico">Evangelic Seminary of Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Advanced_Studies_on_Puerto_Rico_and_the_Caribbean" title="Center for Advanced Studies on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean">Center for Advanced Studies on Puerto Rico and the Caribbean</a>. There are smaller colleges located in the city, including the ICPR Junior College, the <i>Instituto de Banca y Comercio</i> and the International Junior College, located in Santurce.<sup id="cite_ref-college_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-college-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also several technical schools based in San Juan, including the Technological College of San Juan, the <i>Liceo de Artes y Ciencias</i>, Ramirez College of Business and Technology, and the Puerto Rico Technical Junior College. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Conservatory_of_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Conservatory of Music">Puerto Rico Conservatory of Music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Escuela_de_Artes_Pl%C3%A1sticas_y_Dise%C3%B1o_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Escuela de Artes Pl\xc3\xa1sticas y Dise\xc3\xb1o de Puerto Rico">School of Fine Arts</a> in Old San Juan specialize in education that promotes the fine arts and music.<sup id="cite_ref-college_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-college-167"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_and_private_schools">Public and private schools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Public and private schools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>As of the 2022\xe2\x80\x9323 school year, there are 83 public schools serving 24,494 students in San Juan,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> all of which are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Education" title="Puerto Rico Department of Education">Puerto Rico Department of Education</a>. Most of the specialized schools operated by the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico are located in San Juan. These schools emphasize topics such as Science and Math, Radio and Television, Arts, Trade, Music, and Sports, but also include other subjects such as Spanish, English, and Social Studies in their curriculum.\n</p><p>In addition to dozens of state-run elementary, intermediate, and high schools, the government of the city of San Juan operates two bilingual schools, including one sports-magnet school, the first municipal-run schools in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Several private schools are located in San Juan, including Robinson and St. John\'s schools in the <a href="/wiki/Condado_(Santurce)" title="Condado (Santurce)">Condado</a>, Perpetuo Socorro in <a href="/wiki/Miramar,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Miramar, Puerto Rico">Miramar</a>, St. John\'s Episcopal, Santa M\xc3\xb3nica and <a href="/wiki/Academia_San_Jorge" title="Academia San Jorge">Academia San Jorge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a>, Commonwealth High School, La Merced and Esp\xc3\xadritu Santo in <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a>, Escuela Josefita Monserrate de Selles, San Antonio, <a href="/wiki/Colegio_San_Ignacio_de_Loyola" class="mw-redirect" title="Colegio San Ignacio de Loyola">Colegio San Ignacio de Loyola</a>, San Jos\xc3\xa9 in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cupeyville_School" title="Cupeyville School">Cupeyville</a>, St. Mary\'s, Boneville and Cupey Maria Montesory School in Cupey.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Airports">Airports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Airports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Marin_International_Airport_in_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Marin International Airport</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan Metropolitan Area</a> is served by two airports:\n</p><p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a></b> (SJU), San Juan\'s primary commercial airport, is located eight miles (12.9&#160;km) from <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a> in the neighboring municipality of <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. The airport accommodates more than 30 domestic and international airlines and is the busiest airport in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. It is often referred to as <i>The Gateway to the Caribbean</i> because it serves as the main connection to the island and the rest of the Caribbean for the United States and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The area\'s secondary airport is the <b><a href="/wiki/Fernando_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernando Ribas Dominicci Airport">Fernando Ribas Dominicci Airport</a></b> (SIG), located directly across the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Antonio_Channel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Antonio Channel (page does not exist)">San Antonio Channel</a> (<i>Ca\xc3\xb1o San Antonio</i>) from Old San Juan in the <a href="/wiki/Isla_Grande_(Santurce)" title="Isla Grande (Santurce)">Isla Grande</a> district.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Dominicci Airport is used mainly by general aviation aircraft, charter flights and some domestic commercial flights. It used to be the city\'s and also the island of Puerto Rico\'s main international gateway until the opening of Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Marin International Airport. It is now also widely used by the Isla Grande Flight School and Caribbean Flight Center, the only flight school on the island.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Highways_and_roads">Highways and roads</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Highways and roads"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cars,_houses,_street_light,_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg/220px-Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg/330px-Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg/440px-Cars%2C_houses%2C_street_light%2C_man_on_bicycle_and_El_Morro_in_Old_San_Juan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1090" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption><a href="/w/index.php?title=Calle_Norzagaray&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Calle Norzagaray (page does not exist)">Calle Norzagaray</a> in <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Some of the major highways and roads of San Juan include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">Puerto Rico Highway 52</a> (PR-52), also known as <b>Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Highway</b>, runs from <a href="/wiki/Santurce,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Santurce, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Santurce</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> through <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_1" title="Puerto Rico Highway 1">Puerto Rico Highway 1</a> (PR-1), also known as <a href="/wiki/Carretera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Carretera Central (Puerto Rico)"><b>Carretera Central</b></a>, <b>Antigua Carretera Militar</b> and <i><b>La Muda</b></i> between <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a> and Caguas, runs from Santurce to Ponce through <a href="/wiki/Cayey,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cayey, Puerto Rico">Cayey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Cordillera Central</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">Puerto Rico Highway 2</a> (PR-2), also known as <b>Kennedy Expressway</b> between San Juan and <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, runs from Santurce to Ponce through <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_3" title="Puerto Rico Highway 3">Puerto Rico Highway 3</a> (PR-3), also known as <b>65 de Infanter\xc3\xada Avenue</b> between R\xc3\xado Piedras and Carolina, runs from <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a> to <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a> through <a href="/wiki/Humacao,_Puerto_Rico" title="Humacao, Puerto Rico">Humacao</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_22" title="Puerto Rico Highway 22">Puerto Rico Highway 22</a> (PR-22), also known as <b>Jos\xc3\xa9 de Diego Expressway</b>, runs from Santurce to <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_8" title="Puerto Rico Highway 8">Puerto Rico Highway 8</a> (PR-8) runs from Sabana Llana Norte to barrio Oriente and the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_16" title="Puerto Rico Highway 16">Puerto Rico Highway 16</a> (PR-16) runs parallel to PR-1 from the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Juan" title="Port of San Juan">Port of San Juan</a> in Hato Rey to the <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Luis_Ribas_Dominicci_Airport" title="Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport">Fernando Luis Ribas Dominicci Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Isla_Grande_(Santurce)" title="Isla Grande (Santurce)">Isla Grande</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_18" title="Puerto Rico Highway 18">Puerto Rico Highway 18</a> (PR-18), also known as <b>Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas Expressway</b>, runs from <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey_Norte" title="Hato Rey Norte">Hato Rey Norte</a> to <a href="/wiki/Monacillo_Urbano,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Monacillo Urbano, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Monacillo Urbano</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_20" title="Puerto Rico Highway 20">Puerto Rico Highway 20</a> (PR-20), also known as <b>Rafael Mart\xc3\xadnez Nadal Expressway</b>, runs from <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo_barrio-pueblo" title="Guaynabo barrio-pueblo">Guaynabo Pueblo</a> through Monacillo Urbano and <a href="/wiki/Gobernador_Pi%C3%B1ero,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Gobernador Pi\xc3\xb1ero</a> to <a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Viejo,_Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Pueblo Viejo, Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Caparra</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_26" title="Puerto Rico Highway 26">Puerto Rico Highway 26</a> (PR-26), also known as <b>Rom\xc3\xa1n Baldorioty de Castro Expressway</b>, runs from Santurce to the Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport and <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_28" title="Puerto Rico Highway 28">Puerto Rico Highway 28</a> (PR-28), also known as <b>Francisco Jos\xc3\xa9 de Goya Avenue</b>, runs from the Port of San Juan to <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>There are 193 bridges in San Juan.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-172"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_transport">Public transport</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Public transport"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tren_Urbano" title="Tren Urbano">Tren Urbano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Metropolitan_Bus_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority">Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg/220px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg/330px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg/440px-Estaci%C3%B3n_Universidad_-_Tren_Urbano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3188" data-file-height="2393" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Universidad_station_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Universidad station (Puerto Rico)">Universidad station</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>At 4,300 vehicles per paved mile, San Juan has by far the highest density of vehicles on the road of any city in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city is served by five limited-access expressways and highways and numerous arterial avenues and boulevards but continues to suffer from severe traffic congestion.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Metropolitan_Bus_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority">Metropolitan Bus Authority</a> (<i>Autoridad Metropolitana de Autobuses</i> or <i>AMA</i> in Spanish) provides daily bus transportation to residents of San Juan, Guaynabo, Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Toa Baja, Trujillo Alto, Cata\xc3\xb1o and Carolina through 30 fixed routes. Its fleet consists of 277 regular buses and 35 handicap-accessible buses. AMA\'s ridership is estimated at 112,000 on weekdays.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/220px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/330px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif/440px-SanJuan-Condado-IslaVerde.gif 2x" data-file-width="938" data-file-height="450" /></a><figcaption>The T5, 21 and 53 buses pass between Old San Juan, Condado and Isla Verde.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In an attempt to decrease vehicle dependency and road congestion, the city built a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Tren_Urbano" title="Tren Urbano">Tren Urbano</a>" ("Urban Train"). The 10.7-mile (17.2&#160;km) line connects to 16&#160;stations.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The project, which opened in late 2004, cost $2.25&#160;billion and was more than $1&#160;billion over budget and four years late. The Tren Urbano has received less ridership than was originally projected and has not significantly reduced the city\'s automobile traffic, despite a reported 7.5% ridership increase in 2006 over 2005. There is a planned project to build an "interurban light rail system" connecting the cities of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas_Rail" title="San Juan-Caguas Rail">San Juan and Caguas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Increased investment in public transportation, however, has not changed the fact that San Juan is an <a href="/wiki/Automobile_dependency" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile dependency">automobile-reliant</a> city and its fast growth has sparked <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>. As of mid-2010, the government has approved plans for a redesign of this Puerto Rican city, featuring a new <a href="/wiki/Mass_transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass transit">mass transit</a> system, new roads and intersections, and more beach-access points. <a href="/wiki/Road_space_rationing" title="Road space rationing">No cars</a> will be allowed inside the oldest part of city (Old San Juan). The plans hope to remedy previous poor urban planning in the oldest section of the city, the Isleta, while curbing reliance on motor vehicles. The plans for redevelopment also hope to make the city more appealing in order to attract new residents, as San Juan has suffered from a shrinking population over the past 60 years.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Port">Port</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Port"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Juan" title="Port of San Juan">Port of San Juan</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg/220px-Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg/330px-Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg/440px-Lancha_de_Cata%C3%B1o_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2669" data-file-height="1501" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o_Ferry" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry">Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry</a></figcaption></figure><p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_San_Juan" title="Port of San Juan">Port of San Juan</a> is the fourth busiest seaport in the Western Hemisphere, ranked among the top 17 in the world in terms of container movement. It is also the largest home-based cruise port in the world with over a dozen cruise ships. It is the second busiest port in cruise volume after Miami.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Ports_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Ports Authority">Puerto Rico Ports Authority</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/AcuaExpreso" title="AcuaExpreso">AcuaExpreso</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> service in the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Bay" title="San Juan Bay">San Juan Bay</a>, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o_Ferry" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry">Cata\xc3\xb1o Ferry</a> (<i>Lancha de Cata\xc3\xb1o</i>) service between <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o_barrio-pueblo" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o barrio-pueblo">downtown Cata\xc3\xb1o</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_San_Juan" title="Old San Juan">Old San Juan</a>, and the <i>AquaExpress</i> which connects Old San Juan to <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey" title="Hato Rey">Hato Rey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hato_Rey_station" title="Hato Rey station">Tren Urbano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Healthcare">Healthcare</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Healthcare"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg/220px-Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg/330px-Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg/440px-Hospital_Espa%C3%B1ol_Auxilio_Mutuo_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1194" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Auxilio_Mutuo,_Universidad" title="Auxilio Mutuo, Universidad">Auxilio Mutuo</a> Hospital in <i>barrio</i> <a href="/wiki/Universidad,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="Universidad, San Juan, Puerto Rico">Universidad</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>San Juan has an elaborate system of <a href="/wiki/Triage" title="Triage">triage</a>, hospital, and preventive care health services. The municipal government sponsors regular health fairs in different areas of the city focusing on health care for the elderly and the disabled. There are 20 hospitals in San Juan, half of them operated by the government. The largest hospital in San Juan and most important of Puerto Rico and the Caribbean<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> is the <b>Rio Piedras Medical Center</b>, or <i><b>Centro Medico de Rio Piedras</b></i> in Spanish. This hospital, founded in 1956, is operated by the Medical Services Administration of the Department of Health of Puerto Rico. It is made up of eight other hospitals.\n</p>\n<ul><li>San Juan Municipal Hospital: This hospital is operated by the San Juan municipal government.</li>\n<li>Industrial Hospital: This is the hospital for Puerto Rico government employees, whether municipal or Commonwealth government employees. Normally, injured police officers and firefighters are cared for here.</li>\n<li>San Juan Pediatric Hospital - Also operated by the San Juan municipal government.</li>\n<li>Pediatric Hospital: Operated by the government of the Commonwealth, this is the main trauma hospital for pediatric cases.</li>\n<li>Centro M\xc3\xa9dico: This is the main hospital for trauma cases for Puerto Rico and the Caribbean.</li>\n<li>Centro Cardiovascular del Caribe (Caribbean Cardiovascular Center): This is the main hospital for open heart surgery in the Caribbean. It features a hotel for the patients\' families.</li>\n<li>Psychiatric Hospital: The main psychiatric hospital in Puerto Rico. Operated by the government of Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li>Psychiatric Correctional Hospital: It is both a hospital and correctional facility. It is operated jointly by the Puerto Rico Department of Corrections and the Medical Services Administration.</li></ul>\n<p>The city of San Juan operates 10 hospitals. Of these, nine are Diagnostic and Treatment Centers located in communities throughout San Juan. The main hospital is located at Centro Medico. These 10 hospitals are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Tierra,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerta de Tierra, Puerto Rico">Puerta de Tierra</a></li>\n<li>Llorens Torres</li>\n<li>Puerto Nuevo</li>\n<li>San Jos\xc3\xa9</li>\n<li>Rio Piedras</li>\n<li>Sabana Llana</li>\n<li>Hoare</li>\n<li>Santurce Parada 19</li>\n<li>General Hospital (Centro Medico)</li></ul>\n<p>Also, there are 10 private hospitals in San Juan. These are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Hospital Metropolitano</li>\n<li>Hospital Auxilio Mutuo</li>\n<li>Hospital Auxilio Mutuo Expreso</li>\n<li>Hospital de Veteranos: The main Veterans hospital in the Caribbean. Operated by the U.S. Veteran Healthcare System.</li>\n<li>Ashford Presbyterian Hospital</li>\n<li>Hospital Pavia Hato Rey</li>\n<li>Hospital Pavia Santurce</li>\n<li>San Jorge Children\'s Hospital: The most well-known children\'s hospital in the San Juan Metropolitan Area.</li>\n<li>Hospital San Gerardo: Located at the Cupey neighborhood, is a small hospital but is also specialized in psychiatry and elderly.</li>\n<li>Hospital del Maestro (Teachers Hospital): Located in Hato Rey, this hospital is operated by the Puerto Rico Teachers Association.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sports">Sports</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/200px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/300px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg/400px-Coliseo_Jose_Miguel_Agrelot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2237" data-file-height="1431" /></a><figcaption>A night view of the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot_Coliseum" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Teams based in San Juan have been notably successful in athletic competition. The <a href="/wiki/Santurce_Crabbers_(basketball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santurce Crabbers (basketball)">Santurce Crabbers</a> won the <a href="/wiki/National_Superior_Basketball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="National Superior Basketball League">National Superior Basketball League</a> championship in 1998, 1999, 2000, 2001 and 2003 during this period being recognized as a dynasty. The San Juan Senators and the <a href="/wiki/Santurce_Crabbers_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santurce Crabbers (baseball)">Santurce Crabbers</a> were the two major baseball teams in the city, winning the championship of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Professional_Baseball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Professional Baseball League">Puerto Rican Professional Baseball League</a> a total of 17 times. The Santurce Crabbers are located third among teams with more championships in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Series" title="Caribbean Series">Caribbean Series</a>, winning championships in the 1951, 1953, 1955, 1993 and 2000 editions of the tournament. The city has also been the host of events within the sports community; some examples include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1966_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="1966 Central American and Caribbean Games">1966 Central American and Caribbean Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1979_Pan_American_Games" title="1979 Pan American Games">1979 Pan American Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Hosted the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_World_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean World Series">Caribbean World Series</a> nine times.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> played 22 home games at <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a> between 2003 and 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The team also briefly considered moving permanently to San Juan before relocating to Washington, D.C.</li>\n<li>Hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2009 World Baseball Classic">2009</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2013 World Baseball Classic">2013 World Baseball Classic</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1974 FIBA World Championship">1974 FIBA World Championship</a> (basketball).<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Host of the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Americas_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA Americas Championship">FIBA Americas Championship</a> five times (1980, 1993, 1999, 2003, 2009).</li>\n<li>Hosted the very first edition of <a href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Entertainment</a>\'s pay per view <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="New Year&#39;s Revolution">New Year\'s Revolution</a> was held at the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Agrelot_Coliseum" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum">Jos\xc3\xa9 Miguel Agrelot Coliseum</a> in January 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The Latin American Regional <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> in February 2010.</li>\n<li>Host of Major League Baseball\'s 2010 "San Juan Series", three games of the Mets at Marlins held on June 28\xe2\x80\x9330, 2010 at <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>The $28&#160;million San Juan Natatorium attracts island-wide and regional swim meets, as well as winter training by top-rated mainland U.S. colleges and universities, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">United States Military Academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/West_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="West Point">West Point</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Annapolis" class="mw-redirect" title="Annapolis">Annapolis</a>.\n</p><p>In July 2007, the San Juan Golf Academy and its driving range began operating atop the city\'s former sanitary landfill in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Nuevo_(Hato_Rey)" title="Puerto Nuevo (Hato Rey)">Puerto Nuevo</a>, and will eventually include the city\'s first and only 9-hole golf course.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Professional_teams">Professional teams</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: International relations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Diplomatic_missions">Diplomatic missions</h3><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png"
